# Learning Jira: Leveraging Sprints, Releasing Features, Fixing Bugs, and Tracking Development

> Effective software development requires great tools. Features in Jira Software extend Jira so that development teams can implement feature requests, track progress, fix bugs, and manage their work, from gathering requirements to deployment. In this course, Atlassian Certified Jira Administrator Rachel Wright guides you through everything you need to get started. Learn how Jira Software extends Jir

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development) | 2h 43m | Beginner | 50K learners

#### Who is this course for?

>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=14)** You may be brand new to Jira software features, have some previous Jira experience, or have used Jira at a previous company.

>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=93)** Business. Jira projects, formerly known as Jira Work Management in cloud and known as Jira Core in server and data center, contain all the main features of Jira, like projects, work items, workflows and users.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=109)** This type is best for business teams and for managing initiatives, processes and tasks.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=117)** Software Jira projects are designed for development teams and teams using a Scrum or Kanban methodology.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=125)** It includes dev-specific features like sprints, story points, backlogs, and integration with tools like Bamboo and Bitbucket.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=136)** Jira Service Management is for support and IT service management teams.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=142)** In cloud, there's also Jira Product Discovery, which helps product managers collaborate and prioritize initiatives.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=150)** All types of Jira have the same look and feel, but different features.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=155)** The applications can be used separately or together.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=160)** It's also good to know that Jira is available in three different deployment types.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=166)** If you have cloud, it means the software is hosted by Atlassian.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=171)** That means Atlassian is responsible for application uptime, the database and the mail server.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=178)** If you have server, it means the software is hosted independently.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=183)** Your application may be hosted on premises, on a server in your office, in a data center with other internal applications, in a cloud server environment like Amazon AWS, Microsoft Azure, or Google Cloud platform, or by a third party.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=202)** While support has ended for Server, I know that some organizations will continue to use it anyway, so this course includes information for users of all deployment types.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=214)** Finally, if you have Data Center, it means the software is also hosted independently and there are multiple application nodes or instances for high availability, load balancing, redundancy and disaster recovery.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=232)** Not sure if you have Jira Cloud, Server or Data Center?

>
> **[7:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=427)** Atlassian has changed terminology over the years.
>
> **[7:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=431)** As I previously mentioned, Jira Software and Jira Work Management are combined under the brand name Jira.
>
> **[7:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=440)** Additionally, Jira Service Management was previously called Jira Service Desk.
>
> **[7:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=447)** In April 2025, Atlassian changed the name of everything you track in Jira Cloud from issues to work or work items.
>
> **[7:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=457)** The naming change is to support Jira Cloud as the place of work for all teams.
>
> **[7:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=463)** This represents a significant change and will take a while to percolate throughout Jira and the user community.
>
> **[7:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=471)** There'll be areas of Jira that won't be updated for some time, and it'll probably take years for all the documentation on the internet to catch up, so don't be surprised if you see references to old terminology.
>
> **[8:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=485)** This change does not apply to Jira Server or Data Center, however.
>
> **[8:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=490)** Those database records are still called issues.
>
> **[8:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=495)** In this course, you should consider the terms work, work items and issues interchangeable.
>
> **[8:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=502)** All terms represent the exact same concept, things that are tracked in Jira.
>
> **[8:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=509)** As always, don't worry if your application doesn't look exactly like mine, just pay attention to the concepts.
>
> **[8:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=518)** Next, third-party apps from the Atlassian Marketplace were once called add-ons and plugins.
>
> **[8:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=525)** In April 2025, Atlassian shifted away from calling their software products to also calling them apps.
>
> **[8:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=535)** Finally, in March 2025, Atlassian renamed Atlassian University to Atlassian Learning.
>
> **[9:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=543)** Additionally, the online Atlassian Community is now called Atlassian Community Forums.
>
> **[9:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=550)** Both can be accessed from community.[atlassian.com](https://atlassian.com).
>
> **[9:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/who-is-this-course-for?u=76281980&t=555)** The glossary in the next section contains these terms and others you'll need to know for this course.

### 1. Jira Features

#### Software project types

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=0)** - In this section, we'll dive into Jira projects that are specifically built for development teams.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=7)** In Jira, a project is a collection of work items.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=11)** Now, the word project in Jira is different than an initiative your team is working on outside of Jira.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=18)** Think of a Jira project as a container for all your team's work, tasks, and to-do items.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=26)** There's generally one Jira project per department, system, team, or application supported.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=33)** For example, there might be a Jira project called Development to track new features, bug fixes, and maintenance work.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=42)** Each project has a long name and a short name.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=46)** In the example, the Development project short name, or key, is DEV, shown in all caps.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=54)** You can also see a project's long name and key in the breadcrumbs at the top left of every Jira item.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=62)** Jira projects contain work items or issues.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=66)** Each time you create an item, you're creating a new record in Jira with a unique key to identify it.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=73)** It could be a request, a problem, a task, a to-do item, or a specific development item, like an epic, story, or bug.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=85)** Each work item in Jira has a unique identifier.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=89)** You can see it in the breadcrumbs or in your browser's address bar.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=93)** It's made up of the project short name and a unique number.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=98)** In the example, the item's key is DEV-1.

> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=115)** Depending on project settings, you may also be able to change the item to a different type if needed.

> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=123)** And here's the tip.

>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=177)** Regardless of your organization's development method, there are some process-specific terms you'll encounter while using Jira.

> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=187)** The term agile started out as an iterative approach to project management and software development, but has since expanded to encompass other teams that want to quickly respond to change.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=200)** With this methodology, requirements and solutions evolve continuously, instead of all at once.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=207)** Rather than handing off work from one team to the next, the focus is on collaboration and continuous innovation.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=216)** Instead of infrequent and large code deployments, the agile philosophy suggests many frequent and small deployments.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=226)** Another term you'll see in Jira is DevOps.

> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=230)** DevOps is a combination of the words development and operations.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=235)** If the dev team and the ops team both work together in Jira, it's easier to collaborate and rapidly address bugs, incidents, and requests.
>

>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=258)** One thing I love about Jira is teams can use it, whether they use these frameworks and methodologies or use none at all.

> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=266)** It works for all types of teams with different needs and processes.
>

> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=275)** A board shows a status-based view of work items in column format.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=281)** Each work item is visually represented as a rectangular card.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=286)** If you've ever tracked work by sticking paper notes on a wall, a Jira board is the wall and the sticky notes are the cards.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=295)** Jira has two types of boards to help teams visualize work.

> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=300)** The boards are built to use with the two agile frameworks, scrum and kanban.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=306)** Scrum boards are for teams that deliver their work in regular, fixed intervals called sprints.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=313)** The sprints have set start dates, include a set number of work items and strict completion deadlines.
>
> **[5:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=321)** Kanban boards are for teams with more flexible delivery schedules.
>

>

> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=340)** Jira has several software development project templates to choose from.

> **[5:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=344)** Each are slightly different to suit different processes and ways of working.

> **[7:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=445)** All Jira projects in Server and Data Center are created and managed by application admins.

> **[8:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/software-project-types?u=76281980&t=538)** The timeline and calendar views will also show sprints too.

#### Common work types
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this section we'll discuss specific work types and their common uses.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=7)** As previously defined, Individual records in Jira are called work items in Cloud or issues in Server and Data Center.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=17)** Records are further categorized as either work types or issue types, like Tasks and Bugs.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=25)** Jira comes with multiple different work types and your administrator can add additional custom types when there's a business need.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=34)** When an item is created, a project is selected first, then a work type is selected.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=41)** Next, we'll discuss the standard software work types and how most organizations use them.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=48)** An Epic is an agile term describing a large body of work that's typically broken down into many small accomplishable pieces.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=58)** For example, the marketing team wants to redesign the company website.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=63)** Well, that sounds like a lot of work, so let's break it down into more manageable chunks using other work types.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=71)** A redesign Epic might include child work items like improving the product Summary page, updating the site map file, incorporating new graphic files and more.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=83)** In other words, Epics represent big goals and are a great way to group Related Work.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=91)** If you're ever wondering which work type you're looking at, hover over the icon next to an items key.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=98)** The purple icon at the top represents an Epic.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=101)** The green and blue icons at the bottom are for Stories and Tasks in the Epic.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=107)** Now, your application's icons might look different if your Jira administrator has customized them or if you have a different version of Jira.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=117)** An Epic functions just like other Jira work types with one exception.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=122)** In Server and Data Center, an Epic needs an extra field called Epic name.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=128)** It's a short name that identifies the Epic and associates it with other issues.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=135)** In the example I've entered the unique phrase, quarterly dash clean to represent the Epic called Quarterly code cleanup.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=144)** In Cloud, as of January, 2023, this field is optional.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=151)** Instead, in Cloud, you'll see a field called Parent, which is used to create a parent-child relationship between work items.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=161)** Next is the Story work type.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=164)** A Story also called a User Story is a requirement, feature, or function often described from an end user's perspective.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=175)** Stories are commonly created by product owners or program managers to describe a high-level outcome.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=183)** They're often expressed in a standard format like as a user, I want X so I can do Y.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=191)** So, for example, as a website customer, I want a product Summary page so I can see all products in one place.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=199)** Or as a product marketer, I want a referral program so I can grow our customer base.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=206)** Now, of course, not every organization uses this format, and that's okay.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=211)** Sometimes Stories simply represent individual requirements.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=217)** Stories often have a special field called Story Points used to estimate how much effort is required.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=225)** If your team doesn't use Story points, you can also estimate work using time.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=231)** We'll talk more about estimation later in this section.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=236)** Some other development specific fields you might see are Sprint and Fixed Versions.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=243)** Sprints have a specific start and end date, include a specific set of items and have strict completion deadlines.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=253)** The Fixed Versions field specifies which code version a change is released in.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=259)** Sometimes you'll see this information shown as Fixed Versions or simply versions.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=265)** An individual work item can be part of zero, one, or multiple code versions.
>
> **[4:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=274)** Versions often have a specific naming format.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=277)** Tom Preston-Werner, inventor of Gravatar and co-founder of GitHub created the semantic versioning specification.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=286)** Well, this is a recommendation for naming versions in the format MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=293)** Review this recommendation at the URL shown.

> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=299)** For all work types in Cloud, you'll see Breadcrumb links at the top left to see where you are.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=306)** The example shows that this Story is part of an Epic in the Development Jira project.

>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=318)** These Subtask work items are children of the Story item.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=323)** Additionally, this Story is linked to a related Bug.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=328)** Any work item can be linked to any other item regardless of type or Jira project.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=336)** Linking creates a path to follow.
>
> **[5:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=338)** When one link exists, add more by clicking the plus icon on the top menu on the right.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=346)** In Server and Data Center, you'll find the link option in the More menu under the Issue Summary.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=353)** Now, if you don't see these options, ask your juror administrator to check your project permissions and that the linked issues field is part of the project's configuration.
>
> **[6:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=365)** When linking, be sure to choose the best linked type.
>
> **[6:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=369)** There are selections like blocks, causes, and duplicates to describe the link relationship.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=376)** You can also query for linked items.
>
> **[6:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=379)** The example query returns any work linked with the relates to relationship.
>
> **[6:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=386)** The next work type is Bug, which represents a defect, problem, error, mistake, flaw, or any other undesired behavior that needs a fix.
>
> **[6:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=398)** Could be something small like a typo on a website, a coupon code applying the wrong discount, or a configuration error that causes a major outage for multiple systems.
>
> **[6:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=410)** Bugs often contain special fields to collect specific information.
>
> **[6:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=415)** For example, the environment field is present, so the Bug's location is specified.
>
> **[7:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=422)** Other common Bug fields like actual result, expected result and steps to reproduce are present to provide more context.
>
> **[7:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=431)** Your application might have these or others.
>
> **[7:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=435)** These fields help quickly explain the problem and where a fix is needed.
>
> **[7:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=441)** Now, when we talked about Stories, we previously defined fix versions as a way to specify which code version a change was released in.
>
> **[7:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=451)** Bugs often have another related field called effects versions to record where the Bug was detected.
>
> **[7:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=459)** So, for example, a Bug was found in the last release code version, so we'll fix it in the next upcoming code version.
>
> **[7:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=469)** Another common development work type is a Task.
>
> **[7:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=473)** A Task is a simple representation of something that needs to be done.
>
> **[7:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=477)** They're used for anything like documenting a code change, researching a database upgrade or training the new intern.
>
> **[8:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=486)** Some organizations use Tasks for non-coding work and use Story specifically for development.
>
> **[8:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=493)** Others define a Story as something valuable to a user and Task as something valuable to the team.
>
> **[8:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=500)** From Jira's perspective, these can be defined any way you want.
>
> **[8:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=505)** Just make sure you and others understand how work types are used at your organization.
>
> **[8:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=512)** While Stories often use Story point estimates, Tasks often used time-based estimates.
>
> **[8:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=519)** We'll discuss these different methods shortly.
>
> **[8:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=523)** As I mentioned, Stories, Bugs, Tasks and other custom work types can all have Subtasks.
>
> **[8:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=532)** A Subtask is the smallest unit of work possible.
>
> **[8:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=536)** Stories and Tasks are often broken up into smaller child items.
>
> **[9:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=541)** For example, a Task to create a new project Summary page might be broken into Subtasks for designing the page, writing copy, and developing the page.
>
> **[9:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=553)** Since your issues can only be assigned to one user at a time, Subtasks are a great way to divide work that requires help from multiple people.
>
> **[9:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=564)** Just like Epics, Subtasks are optional, not all Stories or Tasks will warrant them.
>
> **[9:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=572)** To create a Subtask in Cloud, click the plus icon in the top toolbar.
>
> **[9:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=577)** You might also see a plus icon or an Add Subtask option in the Subtask panel lower on the page.
>
> **[9:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=586)** in Server and Data Center, you'll find the option in the More menu under the Issue Summary.
>
> **[9:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=593)** It's good to know that you can't Create Subtasks using the Create button like other work types, that's because a parent item needs to exist.
>
> **[10:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=603)** Any child items created are automatically associated to its parent item.
>
> **[10:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=609)** There are also other development work types like improvement, new feature, and other types for non-development work.
>
> **[10:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=618)** Further, application administrators can also create custom types.
>
> **[10:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=623)** It's important to understand how each is used in your organization.
>
> **[10:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=628)** This information should be documented and communicated to all Jira users.
>
> **[10:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=633)** If the wrong type is initially selected, it can be changed later using the Move Command, but try to avoid the need for this.
>
> **[10:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=642)** Incorrect information usually delays forward progress.
>
> **[10:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=648)** It's important to know that different Jira projects might have different work types, workflows and other settings.
>
> **[10:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=656)** In this simple example, Project 1 and Project 2 are both software projects, but Project 2 has additional work types and a different workflow.
>
> **[11:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=667)** If you don't see an expected work type in your Jira project, ask your administrator to add it.
>
> **[11:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=674)** Next, let's talk about hierarchy and how different work items relate to each other.
>
> **[11:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=681)** As shown in the diagram, Epics live at the highest grandparent level.
>
> **[11:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=686)** Stories, Tasks and other custom types are at the parent level.
>
> **[11:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=692)** Subtasks are at the lowest child level.
>
> **[11:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=696)** Here's a practical example.
>
> **[11:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=698)** In the diagram, the Epic is called Build a House.
>
> **[11:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=702)** The Epic is broken into smaller parent items like design house and pour foundation, and the design house item is further broken down into smaller child items like hire architect and approve plan.
>
> **[11:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=718)** Here is the same information from the previous example shown as Jira work items.
>
> **[12:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=725)** At the top of the list is the Epic.
>
> **[12:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=727)** Its summary or title is Build a House.
>
> **[12:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=731)** Next, indented one level are two Tasks associated with the Epic.
>
> **[12:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=737)** Finally, there are two Subtasks.
>
> **[12:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=740)** Subtasks have a unique icon and additional indention.
>
> **[12:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=745)** I like Cloud's list page because it shows an expandable and collapsible view of work items.
>
> **[12:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=752)** There's no similar list view and Server and Data Center.
>
> **[12:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=756)** So, instead, let's look at these issues from the Search results page.
>
> **[12:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=761)** The first issue is the Epic.
>
> **[12:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=764)** You can tell from its unique icon and value in the Epic name column.
>
> **[12:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=770)** Again, only Epics have epic names.
>
> **[12:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=773)** The Epic link column shows that two Tasks are associated with the Epic.
>
> **[13:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=780)** Finally, the Subtasks column shows that two Subtasks are children of one of the Tasks.
>
> **[13:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=787)** The Subtasks also have a specific icon and show a slash in the Summary field.
>
> **[13:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=795)** Here are some of the benefits of Jira's work structure.
>
> **[13:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=799)** First, there's no limit to how many items are created at each level.
>
> **[13:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=804)** Additional levels above the Epic are possible with Cloud premium and apps from the Atlassian Marketplace.
>
> **[13:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=812)** Levels above Epic are often named initiative, theme, goal, or whatever makes sense to track strategic priorities in your organization.
>
> **[13:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=822)** Next, breaking items into smaller Tasks makes them more accomplishable.
>
> **[13:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=828)** This allows work to be assigned to different users.
>
> **[13:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=832)** This way accountability is shared among multiple people.
>
> **[13:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=836)** Next, estimates and worked log in Subtasks can be summed in parent issues automatically or with automation rules.
>
> **[14:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=846)** Finally, you can search for and report on items that are children of other items.
>
> **[14:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=853)** Let's create some sample Jira work items and associate them to other items in multiple ways.
>
> **[14:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=861)** I'll show this demo in Jira Cloud, but the process is similar in Server and Data Center.
>
> **[14:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=868)** First, let's create an Epic in the Dev Jira project.
>
> **[14:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=872)** Give the Epic a descriptive summary or title.
>
> **[14:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=876)** In Server and Data Center, also add a short unique name to the Epic link field.
>
> **[14:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=882)** Next, let's create a test Story and associate it with the Epic we just created.
>
> **[14:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=888)** In Cloud, click the plus icon at the top left of the Epic and select Create Child Work Item.
>
> **[14:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=896)** Select the Story work type, add a Summary and click the form submission button.
>
> **[15:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=903)** Jira will either create the Story immediately or open a screen to collect any required information.
>
> **[15:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=910)** By creating the Story from the Epic, the Story is automatically associated as a child work item.
>
> **[15:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=918)** Let's also add a child Task.
>
> **[15:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=921)** Once an Epic has one child work item, you can add more in the child work items panel.
>
> **[15:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=928)** This method is great for rapid item creation.
>
> **[15:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=933)** Next, let's create a new Bug for a problem detected.
>
> **[15:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=937)** This time, we'll create it from the Create button at the top of any Jira page.
>
> **[15:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=943)** The project and work type created last are remembered and automatically selected in the overlay.
>
> **[15:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=950)** Scroll down and complete any other fields as needed.
>
> **[15:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=954)** And here's a tip.
>
> **[15:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=955)** If you have additional items to create, click the Create Another Checkbox at the bottom of the overlay.
>
> **[16:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=962)** This will keep the overlay open and pre-populate some data for the next item.
>
> **[16:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=968)** Now, the Bug we just created isn't part of an Epic yet, but it's easy to associate it if desired.
>
> **[16:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=975)** On the right sidebar, click the parent field and select an Epic from the list.
>
> **[16:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=981)** You can enter an Epic's name or its ID to find it.
>
> **[16:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=986)** In Server and Data Center, use the Epic link field instead.
>
> **[16:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=991)** If we go back to the Epic, now we'll see the Bug in the list of child items.
>
> **[16:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=996)** Next, let's open a parent Task to create a child Subtask.
>
> **[16:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1001)** In the Task, click the plus icon at the top left and select Create a Subtask, then enter a Summary and click the form submission button.
>
> **[16:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1012)** Because we created the Subtask from a Task, they're automatically associated with each other.
>
> **[16:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1019)** As mentioned previously, you can't Create Subtasks from the Create button at the top of the page, you must do it from the parent item.
>
> **[17:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1028)** Finally, let's link the Bug we created to a related Bug.
>
> **[17:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1032)** Since we just visited the Bug, it will be in the recently viewed list.
>
> **[17:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1037)** Open the Bug, click the plus icon and select Add Related Work.
>
> **[17:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1042)** In the Related Work items panel, select the type of relationship and enter the item to link to.
>
> **[17:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1050)** You can link a Jira item to any other item regardless of its Jira project or type.
>
> **[17:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1058)** Now, let's see all the items we've created.
>
> **[17:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1061)** In the left navigation, expand the filter section and select Search Work Items.
>
> **[17:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1068)** In the JQL text box, enter created &gt; startOfDay.
>
> **[17:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1074)** This query returns all items created today.
>
> **[17:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/common-work-types?u=76281980&t=1078)** We'll talk more about searching for items later in the course.
