#### Using software workflows
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In the previous learning JIRA Cloud and learning JIRA data center courses, I showed how to transition items in a workflow so you can keep status in sync with reality.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=11)** In this course, we'll talk about how workflows are typically used and configured specifically in software projects.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=20)** But first, here are some definitions to know.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=24)** A workflow is a visual representation of a process.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=28)** It contains a sequence of standard steps that each item must go through to be completed.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=35)** Each step of the process is represented by a status which describes a current state.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=42)** Transitions are used to move items forward or backward in the process.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=48)** Finally, workflow transitions have what I call behaviors.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=53)** Atlassian sometimes calls these rules or workflow extensions.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=58)** These specify what happens in the background when items are transitioned from one status to another.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=65)** Let's take a closer look.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=68)** Here are some simple workflows typically used as a starting point for business teams.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=75)** Ideally, a workflow is a high level representation of a team's real life work process.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=81)** This may mean adding, removing, or renaming steps to better fit business needs.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=88)** For example, the writing team may need an extra status to distinguish a first draft from final copy, or a procurement team might need a status to indicate they are awaiting action from a vendor.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=102)** Sometimes workflows contain different status wording, like open and closed, instead of to-do and done, and regardless of the naming, make sure you know how each status is used at your organization and who's responsible for which actions at each step.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=122)** Here's some common software focused workflows with slightly different statuses.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=128)** When items use the workflow on the left, they start in an initial status named backlog.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=134)** Defaulting all new items to the backlog is a common practice for Kanban teams and teams with a steady stream of work to accomplish.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=144)** This status means the item was created, but no work has started yet.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=149)** Think of the backlog as a holding step.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=152)** There's often pre-work that occurs before development work starts, for example, requirements are reviewed for understanding and an initial estimate is added, so priority can be determined.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=166)** When an item is prioritized and ready for work, it moves forward to the selected for development status.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=174)** On the way, the item is usually updated to include scheduling details like a due date, fixed version, or sprint.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=183)** Items can automatically be assigned to a developer, manually assigned or left unassigned until the work starts.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=192)** Users should transition items to the in-progress status to indicate work is occurring and to the done status when no work remains.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=202)** The workflow on the right contains an in review status.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=206)** The status is commonly used for bugs or when verification is needed before the work is complete.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=213)** The type of verification may be formal QA user acceptance testing, automated testing, a quick sanity check or something else.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=223)** It's good to know that workflows are customizable to fit a team's process.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=228)** Different JIRA projects and different work types within projects can have different workflows too.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=236)** Next, let's discuss transitions which move items between workflow statuses.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=242)** Both examples use global transitions indicated by the word all.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=248)** All means items can move from one status to any other status.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=253)** For example, an item in the initial status can skip to a middle status or skip all the way to the final status.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=262)** Some workflows have this flexibility and others require a more linear path.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=268)** Here are two more default workflows in JIRA Cloud.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=272)** The one on the left has global transitions, and the one on the right has single transitions.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=279)** Single transitions mean items follow a specific prescribed path.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=286)** Workflows sometimes contain additional custom behaviors to control actions before, during, or after a transition.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=295)** Here are some examples commonly used in software development workflows.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=301)** First is a trigger.
>
> **[5:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=303)** You could use this to automatically transition an issue from the to-do status to the in-progress status if a code branch is created in Bitbucket.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=313)** The next example is a condition.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=316)** For example, limit the transition to the done status to members of the QA team.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=322)** That way, items aren't accidentally closed before testing.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=327)** Next transition can have a validator that checks for specific information.
>
> **[5:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=333)** For example, prevent transitions from occurring until the estimate field has a value.
>
> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=340)** Finally, there are also post functions which fire after a transition occurs.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=346)** An example is to automatically assign an item to the JIRA projects lead developer.
>
> **[5:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=352)** There may also be automation rules running in the background.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=357)** For example, automation can close an epic when all child stories are closed.
>
> **[6:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=363)** Additional third party apps may also be used to do more complex things like calculate the value of multiple fields.
>
> **[6:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=371)** These are just a few examples, but there are many possibilities.
>
> **[6:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=375)** Check with your JIRA administrator to learn what transition logic is built into your JIRA project's workflows.
>
> **[6:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=384)** Let's create a bug, move it through a typical workflow, and see an example process.
>
> **[6:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=390)** In this scenario, I'll report the bug and also play the role of the developer and the tester who fixes it.
>
> **[6:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=398)** First, click the create button to report the problem.
>
> **[6:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=402)** Then select the desired JIRA project and the bug work type.
>
> **[6:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=407)** Next, complete the other fields in the overlay.
>
> **[6:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=411)** Then click the form submission button and open the item created.
>
> **[6:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=416)** Now the bug exists in the project, has a unique ID, and is in its initial workflow status.
>
> **[7:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=423)** Well, that's the end of my role as the reporter for now.
>
> **[7:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=427)** Next, as a developer, I'll review the item for understanding and assess the impact.
>
> **[7:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=434)** I'll start by transitioning the item to the next status.
>
> **[7:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=438)** If any additional information is available, I'll provide it now.
>
> **[7:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=443)** I'll add the environment where the bug was found and estimate to fix it, and the code version containing the bug.
>
> **[7:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=451)** Since the bug is small and requires little effort, the dev, QA, and business teams all agreed to add it to the current work cycle.
>
> **[7:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=460)** So I'll also specify a fixed version and a sprint.
>
> **[7:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=464)** Now that the issue is estimated, prioritized, and scheduled, it's ready for work, I'll move the item forward to the next status and assign it to myself if it isn't already.
>
> **[7:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=478)** Now, my colleagues are aware that the item is being worked.
>
> **[8:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=482)** After I fix the typo and check in the code, I'll transition the item to the next status.
>
> **[8:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=488)** In the overlay, I'll select a resolution which describes the work done and log the time I spent fixing the problem.
>
> **[8:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=497)** Even if your organization doesn't require time tracking, it's a good habit to get into.
>
> **[8:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=503)** The best time to log work is immediately after the work is done.
>
> **[8:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=508)** The other thing I always do is leave a comment explaining what I changed, where I changed it, and how to see the change.
>
> **[8:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=516)** This is helpful for the testing team or for fellow developers who may need to work on or undo the change in the future.
>
> **[8:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=524)** If your workflow doesn't have a transition screen like this one, ask your JIRA administrator to add it.
>
> **[8:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=531)** Alternatively, add the data to the comment field in the work item.
>
> **[8:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=536)** Next, click the form submission button.
>
> **[8:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=539)** The item is now in the in review status.
>
> **[9:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=543)** Ideally, you should assign the work to the person who will test the change.
>
> **[9:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=547)** It's bad form to test your own changes, but just for this demo, I'll keep the item assigned to me.
>
> **[9:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=554)** As a tester, I'll launch the website and verify the typo was fixed as expected.
>
> **[9:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=560)** The test case passed, so I'll progress the item to its final status.
>
> **[9:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=566)** In the overlay, I'll log my testing time and add or update any information as needed.
>
> **[9:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=573)** It's also a good idea for the tester to log their work and provide any meaningful observations or comments.
>
> **[9:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-software-workflows?u=76281980&t=581)** At this point, the bug is in its final status.

>
> **[5:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=355)** When determining permissions, Jira checks the board query and the items in the sprint.
>
> **[6:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=362)** That means if the query powering the board includes items from multiple projects, you'll need the managed sprint's permission in the other projects too.
>
> **[6:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=372)** For example, let's say a user has the managed sprint's permission in the DEV project, but not in the QA project.
>
> **[6:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=380)** If the board query includes work from both projects, the user cannot manage sprints.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=387)** Finally, if the board query is too complex, Jira has trouble determining which projects are included and can't check for the needed permissions.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=397)** Here are some examples of complex queries and how to simplify them to avoid problems.
>
> **[6:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=404)** In the first row, the query returns all items assigned to you regardless of the project.
>
> **[6:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=411)** To simplify the query, restrict the results to a single project or list of projects.
>
> **[6:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=418)** In the second row, the query returns all items in the DEV project, plus all items in any Jira project with a fixed version of 1.0.0.
>
> **[7:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=430)** To simplify the query, limit the results using and instead of or.
>
> **[7:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/leveraging-backlogs-and-sprints?u=76281980&t=437)** Here's another complex example from the documentation.

#### Estimating work and tracking time
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Estimation helps predict and plan work, set expectations, and communicate scope.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=7)** There are two ways to estimate work.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=10)** In this section, we'll discuss the differences between time and story point estimates.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=16)** As a reminder from the Learning Jira course, time estimates are entered in minutes, hours, days, or weeks.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=26)** In the example, 2,400 minutes is the same as 40 hours, five days, or one work week.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=35)** Time is specified using m for minutes, h for hours, m for days, and w for weeks.
>

> **[9:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=593)** Here's a tip.
>
> **[9:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=594)** When Tempo is installed, you can also type the w key to launch the time tracking overlay.
>
> **[10:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=602)** All time entered is displayed at the bottom of an item.
>
> **[10:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=606)** In the Activity section, just change the tab to work log.
>
> **[10:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=611)** You can create multiple work logs per item and multiple people can log work to the same item.
>
> **[10:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=618)** The time logging process is similar in Server and Data Center.
>
> **[10:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=623)** There's a Log Work option in the More menu at the top of the screen and a plus icon next to Time Tracking in the right sidebar.
>
> **[10:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=632)** You can also log work in workflow transitions and with third-party apps.
>
> **[10:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=638)** Just like in cloud, time logging in Server and Data Center appears in the Work Log, Activity section at the bottom of an issue.
>
> **[10:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=649)** Some estimation fields are queryable with JQL.
>

>
> **[11:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=674)** Jira works best with more data, not less.
>
> **[11:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=678)** Without estimates, you miss out on useful calculations and reporting features.
>
> **[11:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=685)** Next, enter estimates before prioritization and scheduling discussions occur.
>
> **[11:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=691)** This info helps leadership make informed decisions for the next work cycle.
>
> **[11:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=697)** Enter estimates early in the workflow, ideally before work begins.
>
> **[11:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=702)** Next, I am terrible at estimation, so I always try to under promise and over deliver.
>
> **[11:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=710)** Try adding 10% more time to your estimate in case the work takes longer than expected.
>
> **[11:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=717)** If the work takes less time, well that's great.
>
> **[12:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=720)** Now you can use that extra time to defrag your hard drive, refactor some code, or address technical debt.
>
> **[12:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=728)** If you have no idea how to estimate something, look for similar work that's already completed.
>
> **[12:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=734)** If time was logged, use that information to form an estimate.
>
> **[12:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=739)** If no time was logged, you may be able to leverage the amount of time an item was in the in-progress status.
>
> **[12:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=746)** You can find this information at the bottom of an item in the Activity section.
>
> **[12:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=753)** Next, set the expectation at your organization that estimates represent a best guess, not a guarantee.
>
> **[12:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=761)** Sometimes work takes a different amount of effort than originally expected, and that's all right.
>
> **[12:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=767)** Provide your best guess and your accuracy will improve over time.
>
> **[12:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=772)** If new information becomes available, always update the estimate to reflect the scope change.
>
> **[12:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=779)** Making updates when things change is a good practice for other fields too.
>
> **[13:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=784)** If work is postponed, update the item status and its due date to reflect that too.
>
> **[13:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=792)** Next, I recommend logging your time as well.
>
> **[13:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=795)** Even if your organization doesn't require it, it's a good habit to get into.
>
> **[13:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=800)** This information helps show progress and improve estimation skills.
>
> **[13:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=806)** Also, it's best to log time as the work occurs.
>
> **[13:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=810)** Don't wait until the end of the week when you've forgotten how much time was actually spent.
>
> **[13:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=816)** And finally, the only way to get better at estimation is to do it more often.
>
> **[13:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=821)** The more you do it, the better you'll get.

> **[13:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/estimating-work-and-tracking-time?u=76281980&t=825)** For more information about estimation, story points, and time logging, see Atlassian's Agile documentation.

#### Using fix versions
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Rachel] Another JIRA software feature is fixed versions and releases.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=5)** A fixed version is a grouping of work by date or time period.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=10)** The field is typically used to signify items in a specific software release.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=15)** As noted earlier, it's common to use the naming format major.minor.patch, but your organization might have a different convention.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=26)** Read more about the semantic versioning specification at the URL shown.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=32)** There are multiple ways to associate items with versions.
>

>

> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=105)** If you're not deploying software, you don't have to use them.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=109)** Next, it's good to know that the ability to select a version is coupled with the JIRA project's resolve issues permission.

> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=118)** If you can't set a version, ask your JIRA administrator to grant permission.

> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=124)** Fixed versions are per JIRA project.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=127)** If you use multiple projects, they can all have a version called 1.0.0, but each is its own separate record in the JIRA database.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=137)** Keep that in mind when searching for items with JQL.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=141)** Next, sometimes you need to move work from one release to another.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=147)** To do this, simply change an item's fixed version value.

> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=152)** It's also possible for one item to be part of multiple versions, but you should consider the reporting impact of that decision.

> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=161)** It might be easier to duplicate an item and put one in each version.

>

> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=326)** Now, is this a problem?

>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=337)** When there are unresolved items, JIRA asks how you'd like to handle them.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=342)** You can either move unresolved items to a future version or ignore them.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=347)** You can also ignore them for now and use automation rules to handle them later.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=353)** I'll show you an example at the end of this section.

>
> **[6:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=369)** Any version management strategy is just fine to use as long as all team members are aware of it.
>

>

>
> **[6:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=418)** Bugs often use an additional field called effects version.
>
> **[7:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=423)** This field records the version a bug was detected in.
>
> **[7:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=428)** Here's an example scenario.

>
> **[7:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=435)** The bug is in the current code version, and the fix will be made in the next release.
>
> **[7:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=441)** So, in this scenario, the fix version is 1.1.15, and the effects version is 1.1.0.
>
> **[7:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=450)** Some development teams use the effects version field to query for certain defects or patterns.

> **[8:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/using-fix-versions?u=76281980&t=497)** This just causes confusion.

#### Types of reports
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this section, we'll explore some of the built-in reports for development teams, but first, here are some terms you'll encounter in the reports area.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=11)** The screenshots in this section are from server, but the concepts are the same in cloud and data center.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=18)** A burndown chart is a graphical representation of work remaining versus time remaining.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=25)** This measures sprint progress related to an ideal pace, so you can predict completion.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=33)** A burnup chart is similar, but it measures work completed against a goal.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=38)** I find the burndown chart more useful for developers and the burnup chart more useful for leadership.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=46)** Every project, iteration, sprint, or release has a certain planned size or scope.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=53)** The burndown, burnup and sprint reports help monitor scope creep.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=59)** Scope creep is when the size of the sprint increases after work starts.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=65)** It's often caused by a poorly defined scope or set of requirements, a gap in communication between stakeholders, late breaking feature or mind changes, and external factors like industry or market change that the organization must accommodate.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=84)** As a development manager, I was always getting requests like, "Can you add this extra little thing to the current release, please, just this once?
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=94)** It won't happen again.
>

> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=106)** First, have a change management plan to specify the process for requesting changes.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=113)** Determine under what specific conditions the changes are even considered.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=118)** For example, if it's early in the work cycle, if it creates X revenue or it reduces Y cost.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=126)** Otherwise, requests should automatically go into the list of potential work for the next cycle.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=133)** Next, determine the impact of the change from a budget, cost, and timeline perspective.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=141)** Don't forget to include the impact of disrupting progress to evaluate the change.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=146)** Is the organization willing to accept the impact?
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=151)** If so, determine whether you can remove an existing item to accommodate the new one.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=157)** If yes, remove a previously planned item and consider it again later for the next cycle.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=164)** If all the above is agreed to, then modify the plan to accommodate the change.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=169)** It's important to make these decisions based on data, not emotion or favoritism.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=176)** If change requests are frequent, here are some things you can try.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=181)** First, spend more time upfront planning and communicating so stakeholders prioritize the right items the first time.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=190)** Another idea is to reserve extra time in the cycle to accommodate a limited amount of change.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=196)** But be careful with this though.

>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=203)** Finally, sometimes you simply need to say no.

>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=216)** The last term is velocity, which is a measure of speed, efficiency, or how much is completed in a work cycle.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=224)** It's a metric for the entire team, not individual contributors.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=229)** Velocity is impacted by factors like scope creep, time and resources.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=236)** For example, if a team member is out sick, less work gets done.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=241)** Now there's less team capacity, and velocity should be recalculated.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=246)** Measuring velocity changes over time, helps predict efficiency for future work cycles.
>

> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=285)** But reports need data.
>

>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=296)** Without this information, the reports are much less useful.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=301)** Jira comes with many built-in reports of interest to development teams.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=306)** These reports provide insights into progress, release health, forecasts, and more.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=313)** Access the built-in reports from the reports link in the top nav and cloud, and the left sidebar in server and data center.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=323)** Here's a tip.
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=324)** The types of reports available differ, depending on whether the project or board selected is Scrum or Kanban.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=332)** For example, the burndown, burnup and sprint report are all Scrum specific concepts.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=339)** If you have multiple board types in your Jira project and you don't see an expected report, visit the relevant board and then return to the report section.
>
> **[5:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=352)** If you're using a different project or deployment type, see the list of all reports and their definitions on my website.
>

>
> **[6:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/types-of-reports?u=76281980&t=379)** And, of course, items need estimates to display data.

### 2. Power User Tips

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### Getting the most from Jira
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/getting-the-most-from-jira-software?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/getting-the-most-from-jira-software?u=76281980&t=0)** - I wanted to share my top tips for getting the most out of Jira.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/getting-the-most-from-jira-software?u=76281980&t=5)** First, Jira is just a tool.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/getting-the-most-from-jira-software?u=76281980&t=7)** No tool can make up for a bad process, leadership, or results.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/getting-the-most-from-jira-software?u=76281980&t=13)** If your organization is a mess outside of Jira, well, that mess is likely to creep into Jira as well.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/getting-the-most-from-jira-software?u=76281980&t=20)** It's worth taking a step back to improve your process, workflow, and communication.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Frameworks & Libraries:** [[Jira]] (4), leadership (1)
> **Tools:** jira (4)
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)
> **Speakers:** - i (1)

#### Keeping data accurate
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=0)** - Next JIRA loves data.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=3)** To leverage JIRA's powerful features be intentional about the information entered.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=9)** The saying "Garbage in equals garbage out" is so true.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=13)** If you enter inaccurate information or leave fields blank, you won't get to use JIRA's powerful reporting capabilities.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=22)** Be sure to update item status as you work.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=25)** It's everyone's responsibility to make sure the status reflects reality.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=30)** If work starts, update the status.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=33)** If work stops, even temporarily, update the status again, there's no point in using a tracking tool if statuses are inaccurate.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=43)** Also, it's important to enter the right information at the right time.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=48)** For example, enter estimates before release contents are selected.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=54)** Enter fixed versions, sprints, and due dates when items are prioritized and log work as it happens.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=62)** Most dev specific fields are vital for reporting or power background logic.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=69)** Finally, if data is missing or inaccurate, correct it right away, if an item is in the in progress status, but unassigned, update the assignee field.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=80)** If scope changes, update the estimate.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/keeping-data-accurate?u=76281980&t=83)** Don't wait for someone else to update data.

#### Ways to be proactive
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ways-to-be-proactive?u=76281980)

>

>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ways-to-be-proactive?u=76281980&t=10)** Make any needed updates, and then start work.

>

>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ways-to-be-proactive?u=76281980&t=22)** It's better to use boards, dashboards, filters and reports to monitor activity.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ways-to-be-proactive?u=76281980&t=29)** Also, don't rely too much on export functions.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ways-to-be-proactive?u=76281980&t=33)** At one company, an exec insisted that we print Jira items and put them in a binder for review each morning.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ways-to-be-proactive?u=76281980&t=40)** What a super waste of time and paper.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ways-to-be-proactive?u=76281980&t=44)** As soon as data is exported or printed, it's stale very quickly.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ways-to-be-proactive?u=76281980&t=49)** A better strategy is to teach users how to find relevant information on their own.

#### What your administrator wishes you knew
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=5)** First, and I know not all admins want to hear this, but if you hate Jira, if it's a pain to use, or it doesn't work well for your team, it's probably your administrator's fault.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=18)** Jira is very flexible, and sometimes organizations make bad configuration decisions.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=25)** It should be configured to support your process.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=28)** You shouldn't have to change the way you work to use Jira.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=31)** If there's something that's not quite right, it might be fixable with setting changes, or enhanced with a third-party app.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=39)** Make a list of top Jira pains and ask your admin which can be addressed.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=45)** Since I mentioned adding capabilities with apps, you should know that costs add up fast.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=51)** In most cases, app cost is determined by user count or tier, not by how many users actually use it.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=60)** Also, some apps are cloud and some are Data Center only.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=65)** Here's what I recommend before running to your admin with app requests.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=70)** Make a list of features the organization really needs.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=73)** Determine a list of potential apps, evaluate them in a test environment, and purchase the ones that address the top priorities.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=82)** You can't buy everything, so you need to make strategic decisions.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=87)** Also, avoid apps that duplicate standard functionality or duplicate an already installed app.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=95)** Next, Jira doesn't maintain itself.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=99)** It takes a proactive approach to keep it healthy and useful.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=103)** If an item is assigned to you, it means you need to act.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=107)** If it's assigned to you in error, quickly reassign it so the right user can act.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=113)** And if you create an item, it's your job to follow it until the desired outcome is achieved.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=119)** You can't create an item, walk away, and expect a good result.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=125)** Finally, there are some settings that you might initially not like, but they're often built that way on purpose.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=132)** Atlassian tries to steer you towards best practices with the default settings and options.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=138)** A common complaint is items can only be assigned to one user, so organizations sometimes hate this and they do all sorts of things to get around it, like creating service accounts, sharing accounts, and using distro email addresses.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=153)** Yuck.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=155)** When you're tempted to abandon or re-engineer Jira, try to understand why it is the way it is.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=162)** The assignee limitation exists so large items are broken down into smaller, more manageable pieces.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=170)** If multiple people are needed, each should have their own item or subtask to track their work.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/what-your-administrator-wishes-you-knew?u=76281980&t=177)** Otherwise, if an item is assigned to everyone, it's really assigned to no one.
