### 3. Creating Filters

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### Filter overview
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] First, let's review a few terms from the Learning Jira course.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=4)** A query is a question you ask Jira and JQL is the language you use to ask.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=11)** Searching in Jira finds items matching your specifications.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=16)** If you have AI features in your application, you can ask Jira questions using natural language.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=22)** Then AI will convert the question to JQL format.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=28)** JQL means Jira query language, and it's the way to search through thousands of items to find the few that you're looking for.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=36)** But JQL is for everyone, not just technical users.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=41)** It powers features like boards, dashboards and reports.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=46)** If you're familiar with SQL, you'll pick this up very quickly.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=51)** In this example, the query asks how many bugs the marketing team reported this week.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=57)** Any issues meeting that criteria are shown in the results list.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=62)** Finally, a filter is a saved JQL search to use again or share with colleagues.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=70)** Creating filters starts with a search, click Search work items in the Filters menu in Cloud.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=78)** In Server and Data Center, click Search for issues under the Issues menu.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=85)** There are two search methods, basic and JQL.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=89)** Basic mode is a series of dropdown menus to help narrow a search.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=94)** JQL mode has a text box for entering a query.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=98)** The JQL mode is much more powerful, so we'll use it for this course.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=104)** As a reminder, you could switch between modes using the buttons on the left.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=110)** Let's perform a search with JQL and save the result as a reusable filter.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=117)** On the search page, enter a query and execute the search.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=121)** I'll search for items in a specific project assigned to me that aren't done and are ordered by due date.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=129)** Notice that current user is a JQL function.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=133)** I could hard code my name or another user's name, but using a variable means others can use this filter too.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=141)** There's no limit to how many filters you can have, but it's good to share so there aren't needless duplicate settings.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=149)** Next, let's save the search so we can use it again.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=153)** Click the Save filter link on the right side of the page.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=156)** In the overlay, enter a unique name, make any additional selections, and click the form submission button.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=164)** You can change all these details later if desired.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=168)** Notice the page has changed slightly.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=171)** There's now a unique ID in the URL, the name of the filter is shown at the top, and a new filter details link is present.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=180)** Filters are not always shared with other users, so let's change that.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=185)** Click the Filter details link and click Edit permissions.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=190)** The next screen shows that the filter is private.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=193)** Let's share it with others working in the same Jira project.

> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=198)** Don't forget to click the Add button on the right.

> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=200)** I frequently miss that button.

> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=203)** You can also let others edit filter settings.

>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=212)** To share the filter with other Jira users, copy the URL or use the Share button at the top right.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=220)** To come back to this filter in the future, bookmark the URL or find it in the navigation menu.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=226)** If it's not in the nav, get to it from the page that lists all the filters.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=232)** Now that the filter is saved, use it to determine which items display on boards, dashboards and reports.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/filter-overview?u=76281980&t=241)** Since many of you are developers, here's some bonus information you might find useful.

#### Solution: Create a custom filter

> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-filter?u=76281980&t=32)** The tilde looks in the summary, description and comment fields.

>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-filter?u=76281980&t=41)** For due, I hard coded the start and end dates, but you could also use functions and other operators.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-filter?u=76281980&t=48)** Finally, the exclamation point and equal symbol at the end finds items where the status is anything not in the done status category.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-filter?u=76281980&t=59)** Next, use the link at the top of the page to save the filter for later use.

### 4. Creating Dashboards

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### Dashboard overview
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Dashboards provide powerful insights, statistics, and high-level views to monitor the health of the release, progress on an initiative, or your own custom list of important work.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=14)** A dashboard is a statistic space view of items from one or more projects.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=20)** A dashboard shows a lot of data at once.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=23)** Dashboards show counts, trends and charts.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=28)** There's a default system dashboard for everyone to use, and you can create custom dashboards too.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=35)** A gadget displays dynamic content on a Jira dashboard.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=40)** There are many types of gadgets, like charts, graphs, and lists.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=46)** Jira comes with a default system dashboard for everyone to share.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=50)** This dashboard can only be customized by application administrators.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=55)** You can distinguish this dashboard from others using the URL.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=60)** The default dashboard ID is always 10,000.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=64)** At the top is an introduction block and a list of items assigned to me.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=70)** On the bottom is a list of projects I have access to and a list of recent changes.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=76)** The default dashboard in your application might look different.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=80)** We covered accessing dashboards in the Learning Jira course, but here's a quick reminder.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=86)** To see the list of shared dashboards in cloud, click the View all Dashboards link under the Dashboard section in the left sidebar.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=95)** In Server and Data Center, click the Manage Dashboards link under the Dashboards menu in the top nav.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=102)** To create your own custom dashboard, click the Create button at the top right.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=107)** Then enter a unique name and set permissions the same way we did in the previous filters course section.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=116)** Now there's a new totally blank dashboard populated by adding data blocks called gadgets.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=123)** Use the add gadget button and then the other options at the top right to customize the display.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=130)** You can change block colors and page layout, if desired.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/dashboard-overview?u=76281980&t=134)** Once the dashboard is built, click the ellipsis at the top right to change permissions and access other settings.

>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=150)** Here are some helpful dashboard tips.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=153)** First, don't create a giant dashboard for multiple purposes or audience.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=158)** There's no limit to how many dashboards you can have, so break up the information and only show what the primary audience needs to know.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=166)** I usually create one dashboard for a specific team, a different dashboard for leadership and a personal dashboard just for myself.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=176)** Next, some gadgets require filters.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=179)** It's easier to create the filters before creating the dashboard.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=183)** Otherwise, you need to refresh the dashboard page to see filters just added.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=189)** Next, just like filtered and boards each dashboard has a unique id.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=194)** You can bookmark the URL and share it with JIRA users who have dashboard access.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=200)** You can also click the star icon to add a dashboard to your favorites list.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=206)** My final dashboard tip is to experiment with different gadgets.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=210)** There are many ways to view the exact same information.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=215)** In the example, the same filter powers all the gadgets.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=219)** All gadgets contain the same number of items, but the settings and visual presentation differs.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=226)** I like to create one filter and try it out with multiple different gadgets.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/choosing-dashboard-gadgets?u=76281980&t=231)** Then I keep the gadget that works the best for my use case and remove the others.

#### Board overview
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/board-overview?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/board-overview?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] As previously discussed, a board is a status-based view of items from one or more Jira projects.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/board-overview?u=76281980&t=8)** It's an easy way to see the status of many items at the same time.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/board-overview?u=76281980&t=12)** When work is ready to start, drag an item from the To Do column to the In Progress column in this view or open the individual item to transition it to another step in the workflow.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/board-overview?u=76281980&t=26)** Items on a board are displayed in vertical columns grouped by workflow status.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/board-overview?u=76281980&t=33)** Swimlanes group items horizontally in rows, however.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/board-overview?u=76281980&t=37)** This provides an additional way to collapse and expand data.

>

#### Ranking work on boards
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Jira provides an easy way to order and prioritize items.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=5)** On a board or in a backlog, drag an item above or below another item to determine ranking.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=11)** In the example, I'm changing the position of the first item to below the second item.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=18)** As you might expect, items at the top of the list are considered higher priority than items at the bottom.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=25)** Ranking is a global concept.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=27)** Items are ranked against other items, regardless of their Jira project, work type, or board, and ranking is not related to other standard fields, like original estimate, story points or priority, but you can use these concepts together to inform the prioritization process.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=46)** An item only has one rank, even if it's included in multiple boards.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=52)** The display order is based on the item's relation to other items.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=57)** If you change an items rank on one board, it changes it automatically on other boards.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=63)** This means project managers, team leads, and product owners need to work together to determine priorities.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=70)** A single ranking strategy is needed.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=74)** The ranking system is called LexoRank.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=77)** It uses a combination of numbers and letters for maximum order flexibility.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=83)** An item's order is stored as a string in a single field called Rank.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=90)** Item order can be sorted with JQL.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=93)** Use the ORDER BY clause to display issues in ascending or descending rank.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=99)** I added the Rank column to this screenshot just so you could see the format.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=103)** While I use ranking a lot in queries, I rarely display the Rank information.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=109)** The only time I view it is to troubleshoot it, or just to better understand the ranking feature.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=116)** Speaking of troubleshooting, Jira periodically rebalances or recalculates item order.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=123)** It happens automatically in the background.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=126)** The recalculation detects problems, like missing minimum or maximum values, strings that are too long, or duplicate ranks in the database.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=136)** Jira administrators can see the rebalancing status, and check for integrity problems on the LexoRank management page in the System admin area.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=146)** Admins can also manually trigger a rebalance, if needed.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/ranking-work-on-boards?u=76281980&t=151)** For more information about ranking, read the, "How does Jira issue ranking work?" article on my website.

> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=40)** In server and data center, the configuration option is on the top right of the page.

>

> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=59)** I'll select the original Time Estimate field.

>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=69)** Next, let's set column constraints.

> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=79)** In the constraint field, I'll select Issue Count.

>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=92)** In the In Progress column, I'll set the Min value to five and the Max to seven.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=99)** The next setting I wanna change is in the Swimlanes section in the left nav.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=104)** By default, items are grouped by story.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=107)** To group items differently, change the selection in the base Swimlanes on field.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=113)** I like the Queries option, so I'll choose that.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=116)** After changing the field, new settings appear at the bottom of the page.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=121)** Now I'll create a swimlane to identify top priority work.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=126)** Give the swim lane a unique name, and enter a JQL Query to determine which items to segment.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=134)** The last setting I want to change is in the Quick Filter section.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=138)** Some queries are present by default, but I'll add one called Redesign Project.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=144)** The query restricts the display to items that are part of a specific epic.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=149)** Now that the configuration is complete, I'll click the Back to Board button to see the result.

> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=155)** Here's the board after my changes.

>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=164)** Next is the custom swimlane to separate the top priority items from the others.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=169)** The lane is collapsible and expandable.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=172)** Next, the To Do column is red because the max constraint is exceeded.

> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-jira-leveraging-sprints-releasing-features-fixing-bugs-and-tracking-development/solution-create-a-custom-board?u=76281980&t=178)** The In Progress column is yellow because it's below capacity.
